15:54:14","updated":"2021-03-11 02:30:56","type":"photo","message":"“My brother Sid Vahal received a double lung transplant when he was 26 years old. At 29, he passed away due to complications. Sid was a big, strong guy who never got sick. Soon after his 26th birthday, his health began declining and both of his lungs collapsed. Sid fought for his life as he kept getting rejected by hospitals for a lung transplant. He was too acute of a case. They didn’t think he would survive the transplant. Then, Dr. Hoopes, a surgeon, flew down to Atlanta from the University of Kentucky hospital to see him. Despite Sid’s weakened state, Dr. Hoopes accepted him. Soon, Sid was put on a medical flight to Lexington and admitted into the University of Kentucky hospital. It took months for Sid to recover but eventually he was back home and learning how to live life with borrowed lungs. Unfortunately, after 2.5 years, Sid’s body began rejecting his new lungs and he was hospitalized again. This time, because of his weakened immune system, Sid caught infections in the hospital and his body went into septic shock. He went into a coma and never returned. On May 18, 2014, Sid passed away. Sid’s family and friends will forever remember his bravery as he fought a battle against his own lungs. Sid was a fighter and he inspired everyone with his courage. The reason Sid’s lungs gave out in the first place is still a mystery. Due to his unusual circumstances, the treatments that Sid received in order to survive were cutting edge treatments practiced by some of the greatest doctors in the world. Although Sid’s life was cut short, the amount of knowledge that doctors gained from his case will continue to help other patients like him in future. On May 18, 2015, my parents and I decided to start The Sid Foundation. We created this nonprofit to raise funds and awareness for lung transplant research and to keep Sid’s memory alive. Sid was a fun, loveable guy with a big personality. He was also an artist who loved comic books. Inspired by Sid’s passion, I wrote the story of Lung Girl and with the help of an artist turned it into a comic. Lung Girl is a fun and educational comic about lung issues and all of the proceeds from the comic go to The Sid Foundation. The first comic came out in March 2016. The second comic is in production right now. I partnered with artist Loso Perez from Prime Vice Studios for this comic coming out fall 2017! Go to www.thesidfoundation.org for more information.” – Ananya Vahal Ananya Vahal is a writer. The purpose of her writing is to represent the Indian-American community and tell our unique stories through essays, social media, and comics. #IndiansofAtlanta - 22:43:30","updated":"2021-09-07 05:58:06","type":"status","message":"Hindi Hysteria in TN! I see a lot of Hindi hysteria posts among us. Tamils did not have issues in English being imposed on us for last 270 years. Even now, 90% of Tamils don’t know English and we are perfectly fine with an unrelated foreign language being imposed on us. Tamils are proud when their children’s can say few words in English, they spend lakhs of Rupees on English schools, make them understand unknown English/western culture, and we have no issues using our foreign/colonizers language in all the business and govt documents. English has different alphabets, grammar is very different, spelling needs to be memorized, and the sounds are different, however we go thru the agony of making our children learn it. In contrast, Hindi is one of our Bharathiya languages with similar sounding alphabets, similar grammar, similar spelling and culturally close to Tamil. > Should we demand equal status for Tamil? Yes. > Should we have college level education for all degrees in Tamil? Yes. > Should we do official business and govt communications in Tamil? Yes. However, this doesn’t mean we need to create hysteria about a language that comes into use in rest of the India. We are becoming a highly connected world. Our community integration efforts started in March of last year when we hosted the Consul General of the Indian Consulate (Atlanta) Nagesh Singh ji. For the first time over a dozen Regional Indian Associations in Nashville came together in such a big and strong way with local News reporting on it and Mayor Megan Barry blessing it with her presence. Since then we have together demonstrated sustainability of this effort and a common purpose towards this goal by coming together for our Open Table Nashville campaign for the Homeless last December and then earlier this year when we showed tremendous solidarity for the Candlelight Vigil for Srinivas Kuchibhotla. Through all this, almost everyone of you has supported the need for a formal forum to solidify and build on this demonstrated unity that has made each of our Organization stronger individually as well as together. The leaders in this IAN community integration subcommittee have come together to further strengthen this unity and solidarity so we can do more together for our community and the Nashville community at large and thereby become more influential and invaluable as an integrated Indian demographic. When you happen to see any of the people mentioned above, please congratulate them and show them your support and appreciation for their time, passion, and continued efforts. Jallikattu, had kept the Atlanta Tamil diaspora at the edge during the harvest festival earlier this year. Dejected and helplessness, the community was anxious about their Tamil heritage and culture in India. When there is nowhere to go, came the Consulate General of India in Atlanta. A team of Tamils representing the community along with Dr Indran Indrakrishnan met the Consul General Shri Nagesh Singh and Consul Shri R Srinivasan. They spent 45 minutes meeting the community members much longer than the planned 15 minutes. After accepting the petition, attentively listening to our concerns, the Consul General kept his promise - stayed on top of our Petition requests, communicating with PM officials back home and updating the community until the ban was eventually lifted. The Atlanta Tamil diaspora met them last week to thank and acknowledge the efforts of the Consul General Shri Nagesh Singh and Consul R Srinivasan for making it happen, and are grateful to have an opportunity to connect. You made a big difference, especially around Tamil’s Pongal festival. Our initial connect didn't end at that. Our Consul General and Consul kept in touch with the Atlanta Tamil diaspora during the difficult times of Neduvasal / Hydrocarbon project fears also assuring their services at all times. More importantly, the Consul General wants the entire Indian diaspora aware that they are always ready to serve the community and welcome any opportunity to help improve the quality of our lives and connection back home. We are fortunate to have the best consulate officers in our city. 9, 1949 (the ekadasi after ramanavami) in Milwaukee, Wisconsin, USA to John Hubert and Lorraine Erdman. He was born into opulent surroundings, his father�s father being the founder of a large paint factory, which was a multi-million dollar concern at the time of his birth. Later HH Jayapataka Swami Maharaja was glad to see that his name - Gordan John (Gour Dhan Jan) - already suggested what Srila Prabhuapda confirmed, that he and two other devotees were formerly associates of Lord Caitanya and that they had taken their birth in the west to facilitate spreading Krishna consciousness around the world.
